< Review>
Food was good, but service, while friendly was very slow. We had to ask for bread and refills on our water. The busboy walked around looking at everything but not attentive to the tables. They have live music on the weekends and the woman singing when we were there was very good! I'd go back just to hear her. Perhaps if the had more than two waitresses the service would have been better. But again, they were very friendly when they could get to you. I'd probably go back, although it wouldn't be my first choice.< /Review>

< Review>
ok ok ok ok ok you caught me. I probably haven't been to the dentist in god knows how long. At last, those days are gone since I'm a big girl with big girl dental insurance now and need to start taking care of my teeth. I was looking for my new general dentist and to get Invisalign.

I found Blossom Valley Smiles through Yelp and couldn't be happier! First of all, I'm used to those drab, puke color, hectic dentist offices that make me regret even entering the building in the first place, but that is NOT the experience at Blossom Valley Smiles. This office looks like a spa! The environment was calm, the decor is modern, colors are so bright and inviting and its very clean. When I first walked in, I was like "Did I walk into a spa on accident....?!" Kimberly, the receptionist, was so nice and welcoming! My insurance has been kind of a pain, but she's handled the whole situation with a smile. (Thanks!)

On to the treatment! My boyfriend and I were both due for a cleaning so I scheduled us both appointments. Dr. Dong performed the cleaning and he was so informative! He explained everything he was doing to do and why he was doing to do it so throughly, which I appreciate. Some dentist don't even talk to you so... The cleaning was painless. Surprise Surprise (not really), I needed some fillings. Dr. Dong checked up on me throughout the procedure to make sure I was comfortable. Upon leaving, my boyfriend was like "Dr. Dong told me so much I didn't know about my teeth. My old dentist just did stuff and let me go"

After cleaning, I saw Dr. Linda for scans for invisalign.

**NOTE, ALWAYS ALWAYS ALWAYS go to an Ortho for invisalign ** They specialize in this stuff. I had fake Invisalign done by a general dentist and two years later, my teeth just shifted to it's regular position..

Anyways, Dr. Linda is awesome! Again, very clear with what she was going to do. She throughly explained what Invisalign was/ the treatment and what my insurance covered and I'm so happy that I'm going to go to her for my invisalign treatment.  Will update once the process is complete!

In summary, the wife/husband dentist duo couldn't be more kind and welcoming. They are both so knowledgable in their field and I will recommend this office to all my friends!< /Review>

Dr. Linda is awesome and I'm so glad that I chose her for my Invisalign treatment. I vetted/interviewed 4 different Orthodontists before I selected Dr. Linda. When I started the process, I had expected all 4 to be similar in price, so I mainly wanted to meet with them to discuss their approach to my treatment plan and to get a feel for their level of professionalism and commitment to achieving the outcome I wanted. <review>I haven't written any review for anything on social media. However, with the exceptional care that I was given at Blossom Valley Smiles, I decide it's time to share my positive experience with all of you.

Regarding the office,  it is a brand new office located in a medical building with plenty of parkings. Every time i go, it takes me less than a minute to find parking regardless of what time of the day. Given the office is newly built, it is very professional looking yet friendly, clean and net. Equipments/technology are up to date. There's tv screen attached to the ceiling to help make your time pass by quickly  or distract you if you're scared of dentists like I am.

Regarding Dr Dong, Dr Dong is very friendly, knowledgable, skillful, and caring. I'm not a big of dental offices given my bad experiences in the past. However, Dr Dong's friendliness makes my visit very enjoyable every single time. He is easy to talk to. You can talk to him about everything, literally everything. We talked about traveling, food, and kids among other things. With that being said, I feel like I was taken care of by a friend or a family member and not just by a dentist. I find it important to have such kind of relationship with your dentist or healthcare provider in general. It is Dr Dong's ability to establish trustworthiness that makes me feel utterly safe and confident when it comes to putting my oral health under his care. And he does that just by being himself - friendly and humble.

As far as being knowledgable, Dr Dong, without a doubt, knows exactly what he's doing. Dr Dong was happy to answer all of my questions with enthusiasm and passion. I was in the office for root canal. Yes, i know, terrifying right. However, it doesn't seem scary at all after hearing Dr Dong carefully explain the procedure and how it's going to be done. Not only that, he would also explain every single step along the way before actually operating it on you. I find it less stressful that way rather than just laying there now knowing what is going on. Trust me, when you lay there next to all the sharp pointy metal equipments, the last thing you want to do is to picture what they're going to do inside your mouth. He would constantly check to see how i'm doing to make sure I'm not experiencing any discomfort or pain. In fact , to my surprise, I went through my root canal procedure without feeling any kind of pain.

Last but definitely not least, I believe what sets Dr Dong apart from his peers is his genuine caring for his patients. Dr Dong personally sends emails to check up on me after every single time. He gives me advices and tips on how to take care of my oral health and constantly reminds me of them. I truly feel cared for.

With a friendly personality that makes you feel very welcomed and genuinely cared for, a knowledge and skill sets that make you dental experiences surprisingly pleasant, and a heart that wants nothing but bringing good oral health to his patients, I highly recommend Dr Dong to anyone. < userid>
106657027749217460223< /userid>
<user_name>Chapi's Kitchen<//user_name><Time>1605394851508< /Time><rate>5</rate>< Text>
So glad to have an Aldi in the area! This was my store of choice while traveling through Europe. They have lots of normal items (produce, meat, snacks, frozen items) but also plenty of unique finds (European cookies, chocolate, cheese, alcohol I haven't seen elsewhere). You probably won't find everything you're looking for, but there are lots of great finds and the prices are quite low.
Tips for your visit:
CARTS: To get a cart you need to deposit 25 cents which will unlock it for use. When you return the cart, you get your quarter back. When I visited they had an employee giving out quarters to use, but I don't think that'll last forever.
BAGGING: When checking out, everything goes immediately into your cart, and then you walk to a counter where you can bag everything yourself. This helps the line to move quickly.
Favorite finds so far: brioche buns way cheaper than Sprouts (at the same quality), dark chocolate butter cookies from Germany, sangria that was surprisingly good, and a really dark pumpernickel bread.

Remember to shop local so you can support Poway! <3<//Text>

<review>I hate to even mention this because I love their iced coffee here so much I can say it's the best in the County by far, perhaps even in Socal, but their parking lots sucks. I had to admit that it may not detract a star, but it's something to consider.

Cash only, unlike the other locations. There is an ATM in the liquor store bodega next door, but it charges a fee, usually has rif raf around it and the entire shopping center is generally greasy and dirty. Wth, karate school, restaurants and like 25 spaces. I think this was as poor a planning job from 7 leaves ownership as it is from city management having so few spaces. Just check out the dinged curbs, traffic island, lines are barely visible, dare I say even missing handicapped spots... Anyhow besides that I usually get a iced coffee and a taro or mung drink because they are fresh, refreshing and have actual chunks in them instead of that fake powder some places use. Service is very fast and prices are reasonable.

Since it's so small there is no real lounge, just walk up counter, and within minutes your out the door. D√©cor is pretty contemporary and basic, no warmth like the other locations, but they have wood at those. It's a stop through location you really would prefer to drive thru if they had one. Please see reviews for other locations for items on menu, this is the least favorite due to logistics, location and inconvenience< /review><pics>None</pics><Resp>None</Resp><Gmap_id>0x80dd27dac0b6e5f7:0x8ce66086482d3ebf<//Gmap_id></record>
</dataset><record>
<rate>2<//rate>< pics>
None</pics>
<GmapID>0x80dd27dac0b6e5f7:0x8ce66086482d3ebf< /GmapID><name>Tiffany C<//name>< user>
111786517743281339317<//user>
< Response>
None</Response>
< Time>
1473268706440</Time>
< Review>
I expected to be blown away by how amazing their teas are supposed to taste, but I was incredibly disappointed. After hearing all the hype about how 7 Leaves has the best and most authentic drinks, I had really high expectations.

Like what many other reviewers have said - the parking is pretty bad at this location of 7 Leaves. They're located in a pretty small plaza where there are very few parking spots. With the high number of customers that do come to 7 Leaves, it's almost guaranteed that you're going to have difficulty parking here. You can park on the street or do what many other people seem to do and park in the plaza next to 7 Leaves and walk over. The storefront is very tiny with maybe a few small tables. When I came, the line was out the door, so most of the people at the tables were there waiting for their orders before leaving.

The menu is quite simple. They serve a variety of teas including a strawberry hibiscus tea, sea cream jasmine tea, Japanese matcha tea, taro milk tea, sunset passion tea, lime tea cooler, thai tea, mung bean milk tea, and an herbal tea. They also have a variety of different coffee drinks including a sea cream black coffee and a house special coffee. The drinks are not too expensive considering the fact that 7 Leaves claims to use quality and real ingredients to make the drink tasty.

Sea cream jasmine tea: Saw many people saying very good things about in. In essence, this is pretty much 85's sea salt jasmine green tea. I added boba for an additional $0.50 or so and requested the drink to have light ice. Upon first sip, I was disappointed at how bland the drink tasted. No tea flavor whatsoever. The jasmine tea tasted watered down, which was a huge disappointment since 85's jasmine green tea has such a strong flavor. The sea cream on top was okay. Boba was cooked well, but the tea was pretty bad.

Strawberry hibiscus tea: Supposed to have strawberry slices, apples, hibiscus flowers and some passion fruit essence - I thought it was okay. A bit too sweet and too floral-y for my liking, but it is a pretty cool and refreshing drink on a hot day. I wouldn't order it again though.

Sea cream black coffee: This was probably the best drink that we ordered. Very rich coffee taste, and the addition of the sea cream gave it a bit of sweetness that complimented the coffee very well. Because it's such a rich drink, I could only drink it in sips. I do recommend giving this one a try though if you're a fan of coffee.

I tried a salted caramel macaron as well. I believe the price was under $2, which I thought was pretty cheap. Overall the macaron was quite tasty. The shell was crispy, the filling was soft - upon biting, it had a very nice chewy texture which I am really fond of. The salted caramel filling was on point as well.

Apparently you can request samples of the drinks if you're interested in trying them. After seeing one man walk out of 7 Leaves with 6 cups of their mung bean milk tea, we were really curious as to what that was! We tried it - and I can see why people like it so much. Very similar to the Vietnamese desserts; it's rich in taste and very flavorful. It's not something I would normally order, but I would come back and order that drink again if I was ever in the area.

The line actually moves quite fast, and the workers are pretty nice in answering any questions you might have. I do wish they didn't write each order all over the cup, but it's not a big deal.

tl;dr - Overall, a bit disappointed at the 7 Leaves tea experience. I expected more from their sea cream jasmine tea and the strawberry hibiscus tea. Their coffees seem to be on point, and their mung bean milk tea is a favorite. I would probably recommend ordering those drinks instead if you're looking for something to order. I don't think I'd ever make the trip out specifically for 7 Leaves, but if I was in the area, I'd be willing to give them another try.

I saw a bunch of reviews that mentioned cash only, but I believe they now accept credit cards without a minimum purchase.</Review>

This was a totally disappointing visit to an Indian restaurant. From the "welcome" papad to the tandoori roti and main course it was a continuous and unmitigated disaster. See the attached pic of the papads they served. It just boggles the mind that any self-respecting cook would let a papad like that leave the kitchen. And if you are wondering how a place that can serve papads like that do any better on the more serious items - you are right. The tandoori roti was made to a crisp, crunchy, burnt finish, the accompanying gravy was significantly on the 'too much salt' side of the spectrum, and the whole experience eminently forgettable.

The one redeeming part of our dinner outing was the manager/supervisor knocked off a few dollars from our bill. I just wish I had not wasted my evening and the tens of dollars that I did end up wasting on this place.< /text>

I like Indian food. I don't like Ambrosia Indian Bistro. For service, I'd give it a 4 (out of 10). Unfriendly waiter who was very slow to check the table after initial serving and smiled only once. (Am I asking too much?) He was actually on his cell phone while working tables. The service was as close to self serve as you can get without it actually being self serve. (Didn't pour the water, didn't ask if I wanted him to box the food for instance). As far as the food, I'd also give give it a 4 of 10. I had the vegetarian pre-determined dinner. (They choose, but there are other items you can choose yourself on the menu).
The samosas were dry and essentially season-less. The rest of the food was palatable, but not what I'd call good. Also without real seasoning unless you call spicy seasoning. I think you can cook food that's spicy AND seasoned, no?  I've really had Indian take out in L.A. that was substantially better and quite a bit less expensive. To be fair, the ambiance is nice. Of course, I can't eat ambiance.
I travel to Monterey quite often, but will not come back here. Ever.< /text>

< Text>
One of my favorite places in Monterey, much quieter but still right next to the downtown area. Outdoor seating area is lush with plants and tasteful lighting and heatlamps, lots of space, and the indoor seating is pretty as well.

Service is great! Thapa took good care of us, and made sure we were having a nice time. Extra saffron rice on the house was a generous gesture after our huge family meal.

They have a lunch buffet too- the food is particularly well spiced. Gosht Korma is my favorite meal here, the lamb is cooked well and the sauce is creamy and delish. Prices are fair, and quantities are large- share a dish or be prepared for leftovers!<//Text>

1527262316644</time>
<rating>5<//rating><Text>After reading the more recent reviews, I was pretty worried that we would be disappointed by what Ambrosia has become since we were last here. But, no, we enjoyed the buffet as much as we did 3 years, and all the times before that, going back to 2008.

The service was fine; dirty dishes were taken away quickly, our Naan came to our table by the time we had returned from our first trip to the buffet table. (It was unbuttered, the way we like it.) There were 8 or 9 entrees in the buffet, including: Opu (aka opo aka lauki aka calabash) Masala, Mushroom Masala, Curry Chicken, Tandoori Chicken, Butter Chicken, Potato Chips, Dahl, Aloo Tikki, and Basmatti Rice.

The price was only $10.99, which was less than we pay for some Sac area buffets. It may no longer be the best Indian buffet we've ever had, but given the price, service, and decent selection, it's still a great value for Monterey dining. We'll call it 4.5, rounded up.</Text><pics>None<//pics>< Response>

<Text>Ambrosia the name itself does not deliver the quality. been visiting this place since 2013 was OK for the price tag on the menu. Since January 2015 visited 3 times it was total waste of money. Ordered Shahi Paneer, Chicken Tikka Masssala and butter chicken, also garlic naan bread. One of the occasion Butter Chicken dish had more gravy and left over shreds of chicken pieces were found, All the dishes the gravy tasted the same with no difference in texture, taste or consistency of the dish. Chicken is over cooked, chewy and dry. Paneer on other hand was hard and dry. Naan bread was hard to tear in to two piece, when put in the mouth it felt like chewy rubbery as if one is chewing a piece of leather.

Past 3 times this place failed to deliver the quality Indian food to the public ( As tourist is not aware of the quality standard).

I would recommend drive on highway 1 north to Santa Cruz where there are about 4 or 5 Indian restaurants to choose from rather wasting the hard earn money in Monterey.or choose any other restaurant.</Text><Pics>None< /Pics></record>
